<user>106870802795708955110</user>< text>
They should call this restaurant Same Same since it exemplifies what all Americans with bland and no cultural taste consider Mediterranean food. It no longer astonishes me when I read the reviews of people in Brentwood and the Westside of Los Angeles consider this food excellent. The food is fresh but this is not Mediterranean food. This is Mediterranean style food for the unsophisticated palate that is widespread on the Westside of Los Angeles. I am not a Shawarma eater any longer but I have had some amazing Shawarma in my lifetime and have traveled all over the Middle East and this is not Mediterranean food. This is the equivalent of New York like pizza or cheesecake but no where close to the real thing. I had Linner with my sister at "Same Same" last night and she confirmed what we knew from our two previous experiences at this restaurant. Fresh food with no real character and definitely not real Mediterranean food.< /text>

< text>
The Fred Steak from Schaub's is a local institution. It's so go in fact that it surpasses the steaks at most of the local restaurants but you can only buy it here. The recipe is a secret and the copy cats aren't close.

The steak is jet black and not very appealing, for me that's half the fun, shocking guests with such an unappetizing piece of meat. Any concerns they might have had disappear the moment they taste it however.

Guests from out of town now request the Fred Steak when they visit because it is such a treat.<//text>

<user_id>105517910581150391487< /user_id>< Name>
neil thecellist< /Name>
<time>1525137971407</time><rating>4<//rating>< Text>
The WiFi is acceptable. For Irvine, that is mandatory at minimum, especially being this close to University of California Irvine.

Came in here recently on a work from home day as I had an errand earlier that day to run. After finding a table close to a power AC outlet, I plugged my laptop in and started crunching some infrastructure-as-code.

This cafe is well ventilated which is really important during hot Irvine summers, which speaks to how well the HVAC systems are here. That's a damn good thing.

Located in University Center, if you need to stand up for a stretch break, there are plenty of places to swing by nearby, including but not limited to: Eureka, Gen Grill, Amazon Prime at Irvine, Slap Fish, Blaze Pizza, even a United States Post Office! There are options a-plenty here.

Drinks here are ok. Noticed I saved drinks for last? It's actually not anything spectacular but nothing terrible either.

Oh and they take mobile payments here like Apple and Google Pay.<//Text>

<Response>{'time': 1568173853272, 'text': 'Rosie, as you stated above, you came in for a tooth extraction. Your HMO plan was not charged out. We do not receive any payment from your insurance company for your procedure. That is how HMOs work. HMOs don\'t pay, they just have a discount patient fee schedule with the amount YOU pay. Certain procedures not listed on the plan are charged the UCR fee (usual and customary fee). On PPO plans we bill,  on HMOs there is no "billing" the insurance. The HMOs only pay $2 to $3 a month per patient to be on the HMO roster. PPO insurances pay per procedure, HMOs do not therefore many dental offices don\'t accept HMOs. If you would have had a PPO plan you would have paid less for the HMO non-covered procedures.\nYou were not coerced to do the procedures and, as with every patient, the fees are given PRIOR to the procedures and a treatment plan is signed by the patient. If the fees are not to your liking then you have the option to frequent another dentist for another estimate. You chose to have the procedure done at our office.  To offer a complaint a MONTH later after your procedure is done seem a bit peculiar. Moreover to complain about not using sedatives when you made no mention of sedatives at the treatment plan phase is also odd.  The gel is a pre-numbing agent for the injection of lidocaine. It has nothing to do with sedation. If you wanted general anesthesia then you should have mentioned that prior to starting the procedure and we would have referred you to an oral surgeon. I have\nliterally done thousands of extractions with gel/lidocaine, like most general dentists do, with no issues. My technique\nof numbing and waiting for proper anesthesia and then giving a bit more lidocaine just prior to the extraction ensures complete anesthesia and comfort. I recall that we had no issue with the anesthesia and you were completely numb for the procedure. Again if you wanted sedation (to be "out" for the procedure) you should have said so and you would been referred to an oral surgeon who would charge $1500 for sedation alone.\nWe are a high end office.  We are not the least expensive but we are not the most expensive either. We charge mid range for items that are not listed on the discounted fee procedure list. We go by the discount fee list and charge only UCR for procedures that are not on the list.\nHopefully with this understanding of how dental HMO\'s work and how sedation is NOT the standard for  extractions (by the way, HMOs don\'t cover sedation), I would appreciate if you would remove your post. Moreover, it is  SLANDER to post that we billed your insurance when we did not. You can check with your insurance plan to verify.  After verifying, please remove the slanderous post.'}< /Response><time>1568073826914</time>< GmapID>

<Rating>1< /Rating><Name>Tay< /Name>< review>
I just came back from by far the most upsetting encounter with a health "professional" I've ever had. Let me preface this by saying Dr. Miele has been great. He takes the time to simplify complex procedures, and it truly seems like he cares.

This entire review is about my experience with Yvonne, his front desk receptionist. I am scheduled for a routine exam and cleaning. Dr. Miele takes lots of x-rays, and explains procedures I will need in the future. He mentions that he recommends a "deep cleaning" which requires numbing and antibiotics. I ask if I can get a standard cleaning/polishing this time, and get the deep cleaning another time, since I'll be going on vacation next week. He replies and says that he isn't sure if my insurance will cover the deep cleaning next time, but he totally understands if I just want the standard clean/polish so my teeth look good for vacation.

Enter Yvonne. She takes me to a room, lists out multiple thousands of dollars of procedures that I need (including the deep cleaning). I tell her that I would like just the routine cleaning and I'll hold off on the deep one, as well as what the cost of a routine one is. She gives me the foulest look and in an extremely condescending tone says, "I heard what the doctor said to you, he did not give the OK for a standard cleaning."  1) You're listening to a PRIVATE conversation between a dentist and his patient, Yvonne? How very professional. 2) You are completely wrong. I tell Yvonne exactly what Dr. Miele says. She says something along the lines of "I just want you to understand the difference because maybe you didn't get it the first time." Seriously? I don't know the difference between a standard cleaning (which I'm pretty sure is free under my insurance), and a cleaning that will cost me FIVE HUNDRED AND FORTY DOLLARS!?! She walks off and says, "Let me ask the doctor, if he says yes, you can sign a waiver and make a new appointment." A new appointment? I came here to get a cleaning. My appointment was a 3 and this was happening around 4.

She walks back in, and of course, what did Dr. Miele say? Yes, it would be just fine if I wanted a standard cleaning only. But, after all of this, with this woman belittling me, having ZERO customer service skills, and essentially arguing with me as a patient, I need to make another appointment? After all of this?

No thanks. I am taking my business (I use the word specifically, because Yvonne is very eager to explain how many multiple hundreds and thousands of dollars procedures cost) elsewhere.

As a customer service professional, I would expect the front desk receptionist to be just that, a professional. What I encountered was an absolute disgrace.<//review>

<user>114027646903025586854</user><review>First off: dedicated parking right out front. For the less mobile out there this is huge.
Next: sparkling clean modern office with appropriate Covid safeguards, lots of chrome and glass that is impressively clean. This type of Decor shows the slightest blemish, I could find none.
Gina (I think) at the front desk was finishing up with a patient but managed to get me two forms that I had to sign without interrupting or slighting her current patient. Very tactful.
After a brief wait a tech came out to get me. More of the same decor and modern equipment, and a tv hanging right in front of the chair like another piece of equipment. Not a fan of the program playing, but it was at times a welcome distraction. The tech came in and told me the guy that ushered me in was on his first day at the job, poor guy was a bit nervous placing the X-ray plates in my mouth, he was doing fine but the other tech did end up helping him out in the end, I think it was taking a bit too long for his comfort. X-rays accomplished the doc came in and poked around a bit and explained areas of concern. Very concise, and that tv was now a monitor with my x-rays displayed so as to point out the offending areas.
We discussed what priorities are and he sent me back to Gina to set up an appointment for a cleaning.
Gina also said she would check my insurance to see what portion of any procedures we discussed they covered and send me this via email. I could then make my decisions on how to progress with a clear understanding of financial implications.
All in all, an outstanding first visit to Allure Dental. Of course the real nitty gritty is yet to come, I‚Äôll keep you updated on my progress.<//review>< gmap_id>
